## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: The task involves modeling the rate of change of concentration in a chemical reaction, which is a fundamental concept in chemical kinetics. The variables involved, time and concentration, are typical in chemical reaction kinetics.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate of reaction)
- First-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate of reaction proportional to concentration)
- Second-order reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate of reaction proportional to square of concentration)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (A + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Lotka-Volterra predator-prey model: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 - A/c1) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Advection-reaction equation: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * dA_dx (transport of reactants through a medium)
- Bistable reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (1 - A**2/c1) (population dynamics with bistable equilibrium)
- Volterra equation: dA_dt = c0 * A / (A**2 + c1**2) (oscillatory behavior in population dynamics)
- Lotka's autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (A - c1) (autocatalytic reaction with threshold behavior)
- CSTR (Continuous Stirred Tank Reactor) model: dA_dt = c0 * (A_in - A) / V (homogeneous reactor with constant volume)
- Batch reactor model: dA_dt = c0 * (A_in - A) / (1 + c1 * t) (batch reactor with volume increase over time)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Growth/decay → exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x), power law x**c (general growth/decay behavior in chemical reactions)
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(A-c1, 0), piecewise functions (threshold behavior in enzyme-catalyzed reactions)
- Coupling/cross effects → Variable products A*B, power-law coupling A**c1 * B**c2 (coupling effects in reaction kinetics)
- Sigmoidal behavior → 1/(1+exp(-c*(A-c1))), tanh(A-c1), logistic growth A/(1+A/c1) (sigmoidal behavior in enzyme-catalyzed reactions)
- Hysteretic behavior → A/(1+A/c1) + c2*A/(1+c3*A) (hysteretic behavior in enzyme-catalyzed reactions)
- Power-law behavior → A**c1, A**c1 * (B**c2 + c3) (power-law behavior in reaction kinetics)
- Gaussian noise → exp(-(A-c1)**2/c2) (gaussian noise in reaction kinetics)
- Activation energy → exp(c1/A), exp(c2/A**2) (activation energy in reaction kinetics)
- Boundary effects → A/(1+A/c1) + c2*A/(1+c3*A), (A-c1)/(A-c2) (boundary effects in reaction kinetics)
- Autocatalytic behavior → A**c1 * (A-c1), A**c1 * (A**c2 - c3) (autocatalytic behavior in reaction kinetics)
